Therefore, the number of more children who got on the bus than those that got off is 82 - 80 = 2.\nThe answer is 2"

To find out how many crackers each friend ate, we need to divide the total number of crackers given away by the number of friends.\n6. Therefore, each friend ate 5 / 5 = 1 cracker.\nEach of Matthew's 5 friends ate 1 cracker."

To find out how much money Jason made over the weekend, we need to subtract Jason's initial amount from his final amount.\n4. Therefore, the amount of money Jason made over the weekend is 78 - 22.\n5. Performing the subtraction, we get 78 - 22 = 56.\nTherefore, Jason made 56 dollars over the weekend."

"Let's think step by step:\n1. Initially, there were 3 bird families living near the mountain.\n2. 26 new bird families came to live near the mountain from the arctic.\n3. 2 bird families flew away further south for winter.\n4. To find out how many bird families were left near the mountain, we need to add the new arrivals and subtract the ones that flew away from the initial number.\n5. Since the total time spent on both languages is 7 + x hours, and we know he spends 7 hours on English, we can set up the equation: 7 + x = 7 + (x + 2).\n7. Solving the equation, we get x = 2.\nTherefore, Ryan spends 2 hours on learning Chinese."

Therefore, the number of rows Faye can make is 140 pencils / 2 pencils per row.\n6. Performing the division, we get 140 / 2 = 70.\n7. Faye can make 70 rows of 2 pencils each.\nThe answer is 70"

"Let's think step by step\n1. Rachel had to complete 8 pages of math homework.\n2. The number of math pages was 3 more than the number of reading pages.\n3. To find the total number of pages of homework, we need to add the number of math pages and reading pages.\n4. Let's denote the number of reading pages as x.\n5. Therefore, the number of math pages is x + 3.\n6. The total number of pages Rachel had to complete is 8 (math) + x (reading) = 8 + x.\n7. The total number of pages is also equal to the sum of math and reading pages: 8 + x = x + (x + 3).\n8. Solving the equation, we get 8 + x = 2x + 3.\n9. Rearranging the equation, we get x = 5.\n10. Therefore, Rachel had to complete 8 pages of math homework and 5 pages of reading homework, making a total of 8 + 5 = 13 pages in all."

"Let's think step by step\n1. Lewis earns $403 every week.\n2. The harvest season lasts for 233 weeks.\n3. Lewis has to pay $49 rent every week.\n4. To find out how much money Lewis earns during the harvest season, we first calculate his total earnings before deducting rent.\n5. Lewis earns $403 every week for 233 weeks, so his total earnings before rent is 403 * 233.\n6. Therefore, Lewis earns $403 * 233 = $93,899 in total.\n7. Now, we need to deduct the rent he pays each week from his total earnings to find out how much money he actually earns during the harvest season.\n8. Lewis pays $49 rent every week for 233 weeks, so his total rent paid is 49 * 233.\n9. Therefore, Lewis pays $49 * 233 = $11,417 in total rent.\n10. Finally, to find out how much money Lewis actually earns during the harvest season after paying rent, we subtract the total rent from his total earnings.\n11. Therefore, Lewis earns $93,899 - $11,417 = $82,482 during the 233 weeks of harvest season.\nThe answer is $82,482."

To find out how much money Edward had before spending, we need to calculate the total cost of the books.\n5. The total cost of the books is $16.\n6. To find the cost of each book, we divide the total cost by the number of books.\n7. Therefore, the cost of each book is $16 / 92.\n8. Performing the division, we get $16 / 92  $0.1739 (rounded to 4 decimal places).\n9. To find out how much money Edward had before spending, we add the remaining $6 to the total cost of the books.\n10. Therefore, Edward had $16 + $6 = $22 before he spent his money."

"Let's think step by step\n1. The grasshopper jumped 19 inches.\n2. The grasshopper jumped 4 inches farther than the frog.\n3. Let's assume the distance the frog jumped is x inches.\n4. Therefore, the grasshopper jumped x + 4 inches.\n5. The mouse jumped 44 inches less than the frog, which means the mouse jumped x - 44 inches.\n6. The total distance jumped by all three is the sum of their individual jumps, which is 19 inches (grasshopper) + x inches (frog) + x - 44 inches (mouse).\n7. Given that the total distance jumped is the sum of all three jumps, we can set up the equation: 19 + x + x - 44 = total distance.\n8. Simplifying the equation, we get 2x - 25 = total distance - 19.\n9. Since the total distance is the sum of all three jumps, we can substitute the total distance with 19 + x + x - 44.\n10. Therefore, the equation becomes 2x - 25 = 19 + x + x - 44.\n11. Solving the equation, we get x = 30.\n12. Therefore, the frog jumped 30 inches.\nThe answer is 30."

Therefore, the difference in number between storks and birds is 6 storks - 5 birds = 1 more stork than birds.\nThe answer is 1."

"Let's think step by step\n1. Together, Adam and Jackie have 12 apples.\n2. He has 9 apples more than Adam and Jackie together do.\n3. Adam has 8 more apples than Jackie.\n4. Let's denote the number of apples Adam has as A, Jackie has as J, and He has as H.\n5. From the information given, we can form the following equations:\n   A + J = 12 (Equation 1)\n   H = A + J + 9 (Equation 2)\n   A = J + 8 (Equation 3)\n6. Substituting Equation 3 into Equation 1, we get:\n   J + 8 + J = 12\n   2J + 8 = 12\n   2J = 4\n   J = 2\n7. Substituting J = 2 into Equation 3, we get:\n   A = 2 + 8\n   A = 10\n8. Substituting J = 2 and A = 10 into Equation 2, we get:\n   H = 10 + 2 + 9\n   H = 21\nTherefore, He has 21 apples."

"Let's think step by step\n1. The length of Jesse's room is 7 feet.\n2. The area of the carpet needed is 14 square feet.\n3. To find the width of the room, we can use the formula for the area of a rectangle: Area = Length x Width.\n4. Given that the area needed is 14 square feet and the length is 7 feet, we can plug these values into the formula: 14 = 7 x Width.\n5. To find the width, we divide both sides by 7: Width = 14 / 7.\n6. Therefore, the width of Jesse's room is 2 feet.\nThe answer is 2."

"Let's analyze the information provided:\n1. Paige and her mom planted a total of 55 seeds.\n2. They put 15 seeds in each flower bed.\n3. 60 seeds grew into flowers in each flower bed.\n\nSince they only planted a total of 55 seeds, it seems there might be a discrepancy in the information provided. However, based on the information given, if we assume that all 55 seeds grew into flowers, we can calculate the number of flowers grown.\n\nSince they put 15 seeds in each flower bed, and they planted a total of 55 seeds, we can calculate the number of flower beds as 55 / 15 = 3.67. Since we can't have a fraction of a flower bed, we can assume they planted 3 flower beds.\n\nIf 60 seeds grew into flowers in each flower bed, then the total number of flowers grown would be 3 flower beds * 60 flowers per bed = 180 flowers.\n\nTherefore, based on the information provided, Paige and her mom grew 180 flowers."
